		<score>0.7</score>
		<shortDescription>The Crazies</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>The original 1973 film from director George A. Romero (writing and producing for this) was a terrible sidetrack from his successful Living Dead zombie films, I was quite interested to see if they could improve it, from director Breck Eisner (Sahara). Basically Ogden Marsh is a small quiet town in Iowa, the only disturbance recently was when Sheriff David Dutten (Timothy Olyphant) was forced to kill an unresponsive Rory Hamill (Mike Hickman) holding a gun at a high school baseball game. Investigating a pilot's body reported dead in the swamp, David finds the cargo plane he as flying submerged in the water, they may have unintentionally found something lethal. Soon enough communication is completely down, and the town has become more quiet than usual, that is because soldiers have arrived to take all residents into contamination. Everyone is going in to be examined for symptoms of infection, due to the use of the water supply, and those with a very high temperature are most likely infected. David and his doctor wife Judy (Surrogates' Radha Mitchell) get separated because of her high temperature due to her being pregnant, and while travelling for evacuation David manages to escape with Deputy Russell Clank (Joe Anderson). The virus, created for military purposes, is turning people into insane psychopathic killers, zombie-like beings with no thoughts or consciousness, apart from killing anyone they see. David and Russell rescue Judy and hospital assistant Becca Darling (Sky High's Danielle Panabaker) from the "creatures" and the non-caring soldiers, and they are just going wherever they can to get away from the devastation. All the vehicles have been cut off from use, but the ones they do find don't last very long, and they also have a near capture when Becca wants them to get her boyfriend Scotty McGregor (Justin Miles), who ends up shot and burnt to death with his mother (Marian Green). Even though they have all been drinking or using the water full of the infection, it is obvious that Russell is giving into it the quickest as his stress levels rise, and he says he saved David twice, and he eventually sacrifices himself to let the other two get away. David and Judy manage to find a working vehicle, and with a walkie-talkie radio they hear that even the people uninfected have been killed, and there is a countdown to something happening, so they race to get out of town fast. The countdown ends and the town explodes in a mushroom cloud, causing the truck to flip, but David and Judy crawl out and look back at the explosion, and the film ends with them walking towards the town of Cedar Rapids. Also starring Christie Lynn Smith as Deardra Farnum, Joe Reegan as Private Billy Babcock, Larry Cedar as Principal Ben Sandborn and Glenn Morshower as Intelligence Officer. Unlike the cult original you see much more of the insane infected people, there is much more violence and bloody effects, and you actually know what is going on and why, so like The Fly it is a much better horror remake. Very good!</fullReview>
	</review>

		<shortDescription>Everything the original movie should have been, and more</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I'll admit when I saw the trailer, I got all excited to see this movie. However, when I heard it was a remake, I started to worry; which led me to see the original film, and I thought it was decent, but that's where it stopped. However, more trailers and a clip had sort of led me to want to go see the movie. So today, my girlfriend and I went to go see the movie in the theater, and left my expectations behind.In my opinion, this film is simply a HUGE improvement on the original film. Not only is it more intense but it's virtually the movie that the original movie never was- an intense horror/thriller that is also a social commentary on the government, and how they waste resources as opposed to making an effort to take care of the problem. Earlier this year we had the fantastic "Daybreakers", which was a social commentary on the economic state of today, this month we have The Crazies. And the social commentary works really well.The acting here is fantastic. That's something rare for a horror movie- the horror genre has always been notorious for its bad acting- but the acting is surprisingly great. Olyphant gives an excellent performance as David, the protagonist. Radha Mitchell is also fantastic and makes her character likable. There is a good deal of blood and gore in the movie, so the under 15s will definitely want to stay away.I don't want to spoil a lot, but I just want to let you know I thought this movie was great, and a good time at the cinema for sure/</fullReview>
